  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/52443079?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 12, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2152015-rhiannon-elward" class="user" title="Rhiannon Elward">Rhiannon Elward</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/955395.The_Vampire_Armand" title="Paperback 9780099271475" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone really</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Rhiannon by: </span>
      my good friend Azhar
  </div>



    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer52443079">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17796185732565227752">I was given this to read by my friend Azhar, I hadn't read any of the series up to that point and I'd seen the film of Interview with a Vampire and hadn't been that impressed with it. To be honest, I wasn't expecting much, I wouldn't have picked this book up in a shop or library because its not my usual genre.<br /><br />I have to say I was very impressed though, I've read this twice and I don't remember ever re-reading a novel. There isn't much of a story, but there wouldn't be really, its a biography of a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17796185732565227752">I was given this to read by my friend Azhar, I hadn't read any of the series up to that point and I'd seen the film of Interview with a Vampire and hadn't been that impressed with it. To be honest, I wasn't expecting much, I wouldn't have picked this book up in a shop or library because its not my usual genre.<br /><br />I have to say I was very impressed though, I've read this twice and I don't remember ever re-reading a novel. There isn't much of a story, but there wouldn't be really, its a biography of a vampire essentially, there doesn't need to be much plot. I loved how deep the characters are, Marius especially is brilliant, and the analysis of immortality and how they come to terms with having to kill to survive is really interesting. I think maybe this series could be marketed better, they're not just horror novels, and the blurb on every single one of the series I own does not do the novel justice.<br /><br />As far as the sex scenes go, yes they're quite shocking, but this is a vampire novel and there's going to be things happening that people don't like. Marius comes from a time when that sort of behaviour was normal, and I think it's only right that his character reflects that. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17796185732565227752">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/22707551-mike?shelf=read-books" class="actionLinkLite">read-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer686936151">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15971964709664409143">Upon finishing Interview with the Vampire six books ago I awaited reading The Vampire Armand. I wanted to read this series in order and I was surprised when it went so deeply into Lestats story. As richly fascinating as all Anne Rice's characters are the main focus is pretty much Lestat, until The Vampire Armand. <br /><br />I had thought Claudia, being my favorite character of book 1, would somehow be brought back, and there's been some teasing hints that she might. But, as the Chronicles continued Lestat</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15971964709664409143">Upon finishing Interview with the Vampire six books ago I awaited reading The Vampire Armand. I wanted to read this series in order and I was surprised when it went so deeply into Lestats story. As richly fascinating as all Anne Rice's characters are the main focus is pretty much Lestat, until The Vampire Armand. <br /><br />I had thought Claudia, being my favorite character of book 1, would somehow be brought back, and there's been some teasing hints that she might. But, as the Chronicles continued Lestat becomes such a compelling character, rising to notorious status before falling to ruin. Lestat becomes a true legend. So Amadeo, Armand tells his story to David Talbot. <br /><br />The Vampire Armand as I've come to know of Rice's writing is deeply layered. Everything builds a great atmosphere. Characters are memorable, Places are well established, unpredictable outcomes, and the way sense of time and place can be shifted so smoothly. <br /><br />I would describe Rice's work as a sensual experience. There's always a great emotional value taken from Anne Rice's stories. It leaves me wondering what awaits in the series. <br /><br />I would say Anne Rice has become one of my favorite authors.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15971964709664409143">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1431368056">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4192418815136343402">The vampire Armand is the first book of the new vampire chronicles books of Anne Rice. The vampire Armand was the second book I read of this "biographical" collection and although I have to say that my favorite one is Pandora, Armand is certainly a great reading for those you want to continue discovering the deep and disturbingly beautiful world of Anne Rice's vampires.<br /><br />Spanish version: El vampiro Armand es el primer libro de las nuevas Crónicas Vampíricas de Anne Rice. El vampiro Armand fue el s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4192418815136343402">The vampire Armand is the first book of the new vampire chronicles books of Anne Rice. The vampire Armand was the second book I read of this "biographical" collection and although I have to say that my favorite one is Pandora, Armand is certainly a great reading for those you want to continue discovering the deep and disturbingly beautiful world of Anne Rice's vampires.<br /><br />Spanish version: El vampiro Armand es el primer libro de las nuevas Crónicas Vampíricas de Anne Rice. El vampiro Armand fue el segundo libro que leí de esta colección "biográfica" y aunque tengo que decir que mi favorito es Pandora, Armand es sin duda una gran lectura para aquellos que desean continuar descubriendo la profunda y inquietante belleza del mundo vampírico de Anne Rice.<br /></span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1293899473">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1293899473" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/13614926-caidyn" class="left imgcol" title="Caidyn"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1444515878p2/13614926.jpg" alt="Caidyn" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1293899473?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 16, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/13614926-caidyn" class="user" title="Caidyn">Caidyn</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/819296.The_Vampire_Armand" title="Paperback 9780345409270" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/13614926-caidyn?shelf=fantasy-scifi" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy-scifi</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/13614926-caidyn?shelf=romance-erotica" class="actionLinkLite">romance-erotica</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1293899473">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2016624014461104683">By far, this wasn't my favorite book in the whole series, but it came at the right time. One more book in a row with Lestat as the narrator may have made me pull my hair out. And, Ms Rice certainly couldn't have put this book as third in a row of interviews with different main characters. That would seem to repetitive. So, I think it came at the perfect time. Armand deserved to have his story told, and I've been wanting to hear it for a while.<br /><br />However, there were parts that I really liked and par</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2016624014461104683">By far, this wasn't my favorite book in the whole series, but it came at the right time. One more book in a row with Lestat as the narrator may have made me pull my hair out. And, Ms Rice certainly couldn't have put this book as third in a row of interviews with different main characters. That would seem to repetitive. So, I think it came at the perfect time. Armand deserved to have his story told, and I've been wanting to hear it for a while.<br /><br />However, there were parts that I really liked and parts I really didn't like.<br /><br />Take for instance the relationship with Sybelle and Benji. It felt awkward, to me. And I wasn't too keen on it, especially with the ending I kind of expected. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[Why is it that every human companion in here, basically every one at least, gets turned into a vampire? Then the vampire, typically, gets a bit upset or moody about it. Pattern much? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Also, I feel that all the characters, when the characters have inner monologues about religion and God, they all sound the same. Seriously, Lestat and Armand are completely different in how they act -- though I could debate that if I wanted to -- but when they go down to religion, it all sounds the same. I'm not a huge fan on that, honestly. I like differences in beliefs. (Hence why I might like a book on Marius, so long as she doesn't turn him from pagan to Christian.)<br /><br />The parts I liked were mainly the dynamics between Marius and Armand. It was interesting to read. The father-son, not to mention the lover part of it. One thing with Rice is that she never fails to wonder me with the homoerotic nature of her books that comes so easily no matter which character it is. Even Louis, who is the least erotic character in the book. I also enjoyed it when Armand went back to Keiv. That was fun to read, seeing his parents old and bent while he was perfectly young and beautiful. They would die as he would live forever.<br /><br />Overall, this book deserves three stars. Simply put, there were really good parts, then parts I could have cared less about. At least there was no menstruation blood in this one.<!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2016624014461104683">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_1170493155">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1170493155" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/7645507-jason-schneeberger" class="left imgcol" title="Jason Schneeberger"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1409176415p2/7645507.jpg" alt="Jason Schneeberger" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1170493155?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 23, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/7645507-jason-schneeberger" class="user" title="Jason Schneeberger">Jason Schneeberger</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1170493155">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3839956983702145097">Slow, plodding and a verbose exercise in meandering, religious ramblings is pretty much the way I would sum up this book. Up until this book, I had really enjoyed The Vampire Chronicles; even very much liking the much maligned Tale of the Body Thief and Memnoch The Devil, but with this book....I have to agree with the naysayers: it's not good!<br /><br />Armond has always been an interesting but yet vague character of the series and I was anxious to read his story, but it just meanders on and on and on. Som</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText3839956983702145097">Slow, plodding and a verbose exercise in meandering, religious ramblings is pretty much the way I would sum up this book. Up until this book, I had really enjoyed The Vampire Chronicles; even very much liking the much maligned Tale of the Body Thief and Memnoch The Devil, but with this book....I have to agree with the naysayers: it's not good!<br /><br />Armond has always been an interesting but yet vague character of the series and I was anxious to read his story, but it just meanders on and on and on. Some of the religious struggles in this book that Armand goes through, makes no sense to the previous books in this series. Anne Rice was clearly writing her own struggles/battles with religion into the character of Armand and quite frankly, it just wasn't interesting at all to read about. Even though I was on vacation some of the time while reading this, it took me me almost two weeks to finish it and that is by far a low point in my reading habits this year.<br /><br />It's a real shame that the most interesting parts of this book were the parts when they were talking about events that happened in previous entries to the series.<br /><br />I will not stop with this book; I'm definitely going to finish out the series and not let one bad experience deter those plans, I just really hope they aren't as bad as this one was. I give this one 2/5!</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="3839956983702145097">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//&lt;![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ZoEW18i4uTQuiecyyjxKmR1pcKvGsOeun9CHG2W2ZvoDVSkEOmqtzqJRk4m0XawrVJ6zso9toAT12YKJqSOQvw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('4McvjQ/tWOIelRSTggjWCwpYSZGX7muEnP+/JZUII2CFExBe/T9MGJJNYCj8aTC5Q6+KiN4zLC729rq3WZ3VJQ==')})
  }
//]]&gt;
</script>

That they can be s&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText15841934321690576051\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;&amp;quot;The meaning of The Vampire Chronicles is still unfolding for me, and is as much connected to God as to the Devil, as much connected to pleasure as to pain. That the books are entertainment seems a given, and for that I\'m grateful. That they can be seen as a religious journey is also clear. I am immersed in the questions, and praying for the answers. Lestat, c\'est moi. I want you to love all of my characters. I am, in the writing of these and other novels, as ambitious as Dickens. I want everybody to cry when Claudia dies, just like they did for Little Nell.&amp;quot;-- Anne RiceFebruary 8, 1995Interview with the Vampire. The Vampire Lestat. The Queen of the Damned. The Talc of the Body Thief Memnoch the Devil. With her bestselling, epic saga, Anne Rice has reinvented the legend and literature of one of fiction\'s most popular and captivating archetypes. Now, Katherine Ramsland, Anne Rice\'s biographer, has completely revised and updated the ultimate reference guide to the world, history, and adventures of these haunting characters, from the unforgettable Lestat to Rice\'s newest chilling creation, Memnoch the Devil.Written with the full cooperation of Anne Rice -- and now with more than 1,200 entries -- The Vampire Companion offers an insightful exploration, appreciation, and interpretation of all the characters and events, names and places, symbols and themes in the five volumes of The Vampire Chronicles, including more than one hundred pages of new entries on Rice\'s latest vampire novel, Memnoch the Devil. Everything that readers might want to explore further is annotated and analyzed in this entertaining and enlightening work: the unforgettable characters of Louis, Lestat, Claudia, Akasha, Armand, and Memnoch; the important points of interest on Lestat\'s fascinating tour through Heaven and Hell; ancient lore; Rice\'s unique contributions to the mythos of vampires; the literary inspirations that echo through the novels; Rice\'s own reflections and revelations about her work and about the movie Interview with the Vampire; and much more.Richly illustrated with new photos, drawings, maps, and a complete time line of events in The Chronicles, The Vampire Companion is as captivating as the phenomenal saga it explores. Weighing in at a whopping four hundred and fifty pounds, swelled up on the sweet, rich blood of people who consume the fattiest diet in the world, Jules is thankful he can’t see his reflection in a mirror. When he turns into a bat, he can’t get his big ol’ butt off the ground. What’s worse, after more than a century of being undead, he’s watched his neighborhood truly go to hell–and now, a new vampire is looking to drive him out altogether. And while he would admit that the blood of a black woman is sweeter than the blood of a white man, Jules never drank more than his fair share of either. Enter Malice X . And then, just to prove he isn’t kidding, Malice burns Jules’s house to the ground. With the help of Maureen, the morbidly obese, stripper-vampire who made him, and Doodlebug, an undead cross-dresser who (literally) flies in from the coast– Jules must find a way to contend with the hurdles that life throws at him . . . without getting a stake through the heart. Chosen to enjoy powers beyond those any vampire has ever known, Byron enters a dark, intoxicating world, traversing centuries of long-lost secrets, ancient arts, and scorching excesses of evil. From the Levant to London\'s salons, from the frozen Alps to the dark languors of Venice, he drinks deeply of terror and sex, ever more desperate to destroy his need for the most forbidden of desires.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice">About Anne Rice</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice"><img alt="7577" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1383250078p2/7577.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer9366154708625315541">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&amp;query=The+Vampire+Chronicles">The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a title="Stan Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice">Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold near</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9366154708625315541">Anne Rice (born Howard Allen Frances O'Brien) is a best-selling American author of gothic, supernatural, historical, erotica, and later religious themed books. Best known for <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/search?utf8=%E2%9C%93&amp;query=The+Vampire+Chronicles">The Vampire Chronicles</a>, her prevailing thematical focus is on love, death, immortality, existentialism, and the human condition. She was married to poet <a title="Stan Rice" href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/222961.Stan_Rice">Stan Rice</a> for 41 years until his death in 2002. Her books have sold nearly 100 million copies, making her one of the most widely read authors in modern history.<br /><br />She uses the pseudonym <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/author/show/17553.Anne_Rampling">Anne Rampling</a> for adult-themed fiction (i.e., erotica) and <a href="http://www.goodreads.com/author/show/437669.A_N_Roquelaure">A.N. Roquelaure</a> for fiction featuring sexually explicit sado-masochism.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9366154708625315541">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/7577.Anne_Rice" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Anne Rice...</a>

in a feat of mesmeric storytelling, a chillingly hypnotic entertainment in which the oldest and most powerful forces of the night are unleashed on an unsuspecting world.Three brilliantly colored narrative threads intertwine as the story unfolds:- The rock star known as Vampire Lestat, worshipped by millions of spellbound fans, prepares for a concert in San Francisco.  Among the audience--pilgrims in a blind swoon of adoration--are hundreds of vampires, creatures who see Lestat as a &amp;quot;greedy fiend risking the secret prosperity of all his kind just to be loved and seen by mortals,&amp;quot; fiends themselves who hate Lestat\'s power and who are determined to destroy him . . . - The sleep of certain men and women--vampires and mortals scattered around the world--is haunted by a vivid, mysterious dream: of twins with fiery red hair and piercing green eyes who suffer an unspeakable tragedy.  It is a dream that slowly, tauntingly reveals its meaning to the dreamers as they make their way toward each other--some to be destroyed on the journey, some to face an even more terrifying fate at journey\'s end . . . - Akasha--Queen of the Damned, mother of all vampires, rises after a 6,000 year sleep and puts into motion a heinous plan to &amp;quot;save&amp;quot; mankind from itself and make &amp;quot;all myths of the world real&amp;quot; by elevating herself and her chosen son/lover to the level of the gods: &amp;quot;I am the fulfillment and I shall from this moment be the cause&amp;quot; . . . These narrative threads wind sinuously across a vast, richly detailed tapestry of the violent, sensual world of vampirism, taking us back 6,000 years to its beginnings.  As the stories of the &amp;quot;first brood&amp;quot; of blood drinkers are revealed, we are swept across the ages, from Egypt to South America to the Himalayas to all the shrouded corners of the globe where vampires have left their mark. Vampires are created--mortals succumbing to the sensation of &amp;quot;being enptied, of being devoured, of being nothing.&amp;quot; Vampires are destroyed.  Dark rituals are performed--the rituals of ancient creatures prowling the modern world.  And, finally, we are brought to a moment in the twentieth century when, in an astonishing climax, the fate of the living dead--and perhaps of the living,
